    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer17939940909536048542">Self-proclaimed fat girl Willowdean Dickson (dubbed “Dumplin’” by her former beauty queen mom) has always been at home in her own skin.   <span id="freeText17939940909536048542" style="display:none">Self-proclaimed fat girl Willowdean Dickson (dubbed “Dumplin’” by her former beauty queen mom) has always been at home in her own skin. Her thoughts on having the ultimate bikini body? Put a bikini on your body. With her all-American beauty best friend, Ellen, by her side, things have always worked…until Will takes a job at Harpy’s, the local fast-food joint. There she meets Private School Bo, a hot former jock. Will isn’t surprised to find herself attracted to Bo. But she is surprised when he seems to like her back.<br /><br />Instead of finding new heights of self-assurance in her relationship with Bo, Will starts to doubt herself. So she sets out to take back her confidence by doing the most horrifying thing she can imagine: entering the Miss Clover City beauty pageant—along with several other unlikely candidates—to show the world that she deserves to be up there as much as any twiggy girl does. Along the way, she’ll shock the hell out of Clover City—and maybe herself most of all.<br /><br />With starry Texas nights, red candy suckers, Dolly Parton songs, and a wildly unforgettable heroine—<i>Dumplin’</i> is guaranteed to steal your heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17939940909536048542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No. As I stated in my review, it's about finding that inner confidence and loving who you are no matter what shape, size or what you look like. The ma<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No. As I stated in my review, it's about finding that inner confidence and loving who you are no matter what shape, size or what you look like. The main character does discuss her issues with her full figured appearance but surprisingly she doesn't let it consume her and finds a way to make it work to her advantage.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1314553375" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1314553375" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1314553375?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1314553375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7166623932853744481">This book is a <b>hypocritical mess</b>. There are three main things wrong with it:<br/><br/>1. It was boring<br/>2. It's not body-positive for a book that's about body positivity<br/>3. A love triangle (boo! hiss!)<br/><br/>Doesn't that defeat the purpose of this book? I would say it does. This book is vastly inferior to the spectacular <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18245617-future-perfect' rel='nofollow noopener'>Future Perfect</a>, which sends the message of being comfortable in your own body in a far better way.<br/><br/>The main character in this book is fat. She is also an insecure, judgmental snit. Look, I get that </span>
  <span id="freeText7166623932853744481" style="display:none">This book is a <b>hypocritical mess</b>. There are three main things wrong with it:<br /><br />1. It was boring<br />2. It's not body-positive for a book that's about body positivity<br />3. A love triangle (boo! hiss!)<br /><br />Doesn't that defeat the purpose of this book? I would say it does. This book is vastly inferior to the spectacular <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18245617-future-perfect" rel="nofollow noopener">Future Perfect</a>, which sends the message of being comfortable in your own body in a far better way.<br /><br />The main character in this book is fat. She is also an insecure, judgmental snit. Look, I get that characters aren't perfect. I'm not perfect (gasp, horror, etc.) but <b>characters should elicit sympathy in a reader</b> and it is supremely hard to do that when <b>the main character is constantly judging others whom she deem to be lesser and uglier and fatter than she is.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I’m fat, but Millie’s the type of fat that requires elastic waist pants because they don’t make pants with buttons and zippers in her size. Her eyes are too close together and her nose pinches up at the end. She wears shirts with puppies and kittens and not in an ironic way.</i>
</blockquote>It's hard to send a message of body positivity and acceptance in others when the main character tends to <b>skinny-shame</b>, however contrite she feels about it.<br /><br />The main character is an <b>insecure mess</b>, and not in a good way.<blockquote>
  <i>Millie and Amanda together are basically one giant moving target that says MAKE FUN OF US.<br /><br />Amanda’s legs are uneven, so she wears these thick corrective shoes that make her look like Frankenstein. (At least according to Patrick Thomas.) When we were kids and she didn’t have her shoes yet, Amanda just limped around, her hips swiveling up and down with each step. She never seemed bothered, but that didn’t stop people from staring. The nickname thing is pretty lame if you think about it. Frankenstein was the doctor, not the monster.</i>
</blockquote>I don't sympathize with her. I want her to grow the fuck up and get over it. Again, a book should make me feel for the character; the only thing the interestingly named Willowdean does for me is grate on my nerves. It's not that I have a problem with her insecurity, it's that it is a constant part of her life and her narrative for a book that promises me a tough girl. It's that <b>she is slyly judgmental against all the skinny pageant girls.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Cliques of girls sit at round tables with white tablecloths, the same ones my mother ironed in our living room last night. The legacy girls with mothers and sisters who have been crowned. Athletes trying to beef up their college résumés. The cheer table, which consists of anyone who does anything at a football game that doesn’t include a ball. And the theater and the choir girls, of course. All of them wear dresses. Like, Easter dresses. Precious little garden dresses with matching cardigans. While we are wearing nothing more than jeans and T-shirts.</i>
</blockquote>Because she's so superior, being normal. Being fat.<br /><br />Willow is a supreme bitch to her beautiful, slim best friend, El. When Willow decides to send a message and enter a pageant (with odds of zero in her favor), El decides to join forces with her. United we stand, right? Wrong. Having her best friend with her is the last thing Willow wants.<blockquote>
  <i>“Have you thought about the fact that I feel as out of place here as you do?”<br /><br />“You have to back out. El, for me, you’ve got to. Let me have this one thing.”<br /><br />“What? Let you have what? You can’t pick and choose who joins the revolution.” She makes air quotes as she says “revolution.”<br /><br />I hear the logic in her voice. I recognize the truth there. But if El entered, she could really win. And that’s why she could ruin this.</i>
</blockquote>It's like El said. <b>You can't pick and choose your message.</b><br /><br />Furthermore, nothing happens in this book. Willow goes about her life. Willow meets people. Willow talks to people. Willow has a crush. All that's fine and good in the hands of a good writer, because after all, the majority of contemporaries are just about people going about their lives. The writing in this book does brilliant to make this book shine. You could skip half the book and not miss much. Most of the book isn't worth reading anyway.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7166623932853744481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1267675289" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1267675289" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1267675289?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1267675289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11634425312681388096"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18304322.Dumplin_' title='Dumplin' by Julie Murphy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dumplin'</a> might be the perfect example of why I don't tend to read light-hearted, fluffy contemporaries. <br/><br/>Occasionally, my foray into this sub-genre ends with surprising new favourites like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19547856.Simon_vs__the_Homo_Sapiens_Agenda' title='Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda by Becky Albertalli' rel='nofollow noopener'>Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda</a>, but mostly I'm left feeling a little underwhelmed. Many times, I'm thinking "yeah, that was quite a nice book" or "that had an important message" but I don't feel any emotional connection to it.<br/><br/><b>The thing about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18304322.Dumplin_' title='Dumplin' by Julie Murphy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dumplin'</a> is that it contains a great message</b>. Willowdean "Dumplin'"</span>
  <span id="freeText11634425312681388096" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18304322.Dumplin_" title="Dumplin' by Julie Murphy" rel="nofollow noopener">Dumplin'</a> might be the perfect example of why I don't tend to read light-hearted, fluffy contemporaries. <br /><br />Occasionally, my foray into this sub-genre ends with surprising new favourites like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19547856.Simon_vs__the_Homo_Sapiens_Agenda" title="Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda by Becky Albertalli" rel="nofollow noopener">Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda</a>, but mostly I'm left feeling a little underwhelmed. Many times, I'm thinking "yeah, that was quite a nice book" or "that had an important message" but I don't feel any emotional connection to it.<br /><br /><b>The thing about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18304322.Dumplin_" title="Dumplin' by Julie Murphy" rel="nofollow noopener">Dumplin'</a> is that it contains a great message</b>. Willowdean "Dumplin'" Dickson is fat - and no, that is NOT an insult to her. She deals with other people's judgey eyes but, for the most part, she doesn't care. She's happy with who she is and other people can go screw themselves if they think differently.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>I know that fat girls are supposed to be allergic to pools or whatever, but I love swimming. I mean, I’m not stupid. I know people stare, but they can’t blame me for wanting to cool off. And why should it even matter? What about having huge, bumpy thighs means that I need to apologize?</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>This is an extremely body-positive book</b>, which is a great thing. It's very much about breaking down stereotypes, learning not to judge, and learning to love yourself. Willowdean is not perfect and sometimes gets judgmental too when put in a bad mood, but she chastises herself for it:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“And who the hell was that twiggy bitch?” As soon as it’s out of my mouth I regret it. All my life I’ve had a body worth commenting on and if living in my skin has taught me anything it’s that if it’s not your body, it’s not yours to comment on. Fat. Skinny. Short. Tall. It doesn’t matter.</i>
</blockquote><br />As well as this, <b>it's very sex-positive too</b>. Willow is a virgin but she offers support to her best friend when she chooses to sleep with her boyfriend and it doesn't turn into a drama-filled horror story when she finally does. <br /><br />Murphy introduces complex relationships between Willow and her friends and family. She also opened up an all new can of worms when she decided to include so many references to my beloved Dolly Parton (yes, I love her! yes, I have seen her in concert! she is a goddess of joy and inspiration). But more about that later.<br /><br />But I just think a book needs to have a little more than this to draw you in - it needs to be moving, thrilling, exciting or (as I thought this would be) funny. And it's not really any of those. I never laughed, teared up, realized something new, or wondered what would happen next. The pacing is slow and the actual pageant doesn't rear its head until the second half of the book. <b>I like this book mostly because I'm glad a book with this message exists.</b><br /><br />Also, I understand why Murphy included the romance, but I never felt any chemistry between Willowdean and Bo, AND it did seem a little bit like wish fulfillment. I know the author wanted to show that big girls are not unattractive and have normal relationships and dates with guys, but did it really have to be a drop-dead gorgeous jock type? I had to roll my eyes at that one.<br /><br />But one last thing - <b>DOLLY PARTON</b>. If she is not currently your go-to playlist when you need a pick-me-up, you seriously need to get on it! Here, I'll help:<br /><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=8sXuQqk781I" rel="nofollow noopener">Wildflowers</a><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=On01p9_tIvE" rel="nofollow noopener">Backwoods Barbie</a><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UvbGz3eQpZo" rel="nofollow noopener">Better Get to Livin'</a><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5Hl-yIqeWaQ" rel="nofollow noopener">Eagle When She Flies</a><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=b723maOPOaU" rel="nofollow noopener">Just Because I'm a Woman</a> (What a feminist!)<br /><blockquote>
  <i>I've always been misunderstood because of how I look.<br />Don't judge me by the cover 'cause I'm a real good book.</i>
</blockquote><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11634425312681388096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_699321746" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/699321746" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/699321746?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2015-favorites">2015-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=hilarious">hilarious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=made-my-heart-hurt">made-my-heart-hurt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=to-review">to-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2015-publication">2015-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=harpercollins">harpercollins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=own-dtb-tbr">own-dtb-tbr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer699321746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1996047509088457271">If this book were a movie, we'd all be at Julie Murphy's slumber party piled in front of the TV in our jammies, both screaming with laughter and clutching each other the minute someone leaned in for a kiss. <br/><br/>This book is: Hilarious. Quietly poignant. Provocative. <br/><br/>This book contains: <b>Nuanced friendships</b> and complex families. Romantic moments <b>as sweet as puppy dog kisses</b>. Lots of Dolly Parton songs. References to awesome books. <br/><br/>And it's so great to find a book that is <b>fiercely positive</b>, most especi</span>
  <span id="freeText1996047509088457271" style="display:none">If this book were a movie, we'd all be at Julie Murphy's slumber party piled in front of the TV in our jammies, both screaming with laughter and clutching each other the minute someone leaned in for a kiss. <br /><br />This book is: Hilarious. Quietly poignant. Provocative. <br /><br />This book contains: <b>Nuanced friendships</b> and complex families. Romantic moments <b>as sweet as puppy dog kisses</b>. Lots of Dolly Parton songs. References to awesome books. <br /><br />And it's so great to find a book that is <b>fiercely positive</b>, most especially about <b>body image</b>, identity, and self-love. The best stories let you live for awhile in someone else's skin and allow you to experience the world in way you haven't before. Being inside Willowdean Dickson's head is a joy, not only because it's so easy to sympathize with and relate to her, but also because that <b>sassy Texas attitude makes her so damned funny.</b> <br /><br />I loved the everyday experiences of the first part of the book, when Will is going to work and school and dealing with drifting apart with her BFF, and struggling with her sadness over her aunt's recent death and her mom's imperviousness to her feelings. Not to mention the KISSES. I wasn't as into the pageant part that dominated the second half, but it was handled in a way that felt both realistic and satisfying. (Thank heaven it didn't feel false or manipulative--or even worse, zany.) True story: looking up "pageant mums" will both horrify and delight you. <br /><br />I'm also super jealous of all the kids who get to frequent Julie Murphy's branch, because she's got to be the coolest library lady that ever was. I've seen photos of that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19543.Where_the_Wild_Things_Are" title="Where the Wild Things Are by Maurice Sendak" rel="nofollow noopener">Where the Wild Things Are</a> tattoo. <br /><br />Um...a more polished review at some point when it's not 3:30 in the morning. But seriously, put this one on your list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1996047509088457271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2717446263" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2717446263" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77602709-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519184646p2/77602709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2717446263?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/77602709-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2717446263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11202269094223075863"><b>3</b>/5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️ <br/><blockquote>“I guess sometimes the perfection we perceive in others is made up of a whole bunch of tiny imperfections, because some days the damn dress just won't zip.”</blockquote> <br/><br/>Look, 3 stars isn't a good rating nor a bad rating. But the issues I had with this book sometimes overcame the good stuff. I can't stop comparing the book to the Netflix movie based on it I saw beforehand (yes, I have watched the movie adaptation before reading the book yet again, AND STILL YOU HAVEN'T SLAYED ME YOU BUFFOONS</span>
  <span id="freeText11202269094223075863" style="display:none"><b>3</b>/5 Stars ⭐️⭐️⭐️ <br /><blockquote>“I guess sometimes the perfection we perceive in others is made up of a whole bunch of tiny imperfections, because some days the damn dress just won't zip.”</blockquote> <br /><br />Look, 3 stars isn't a good rating nor a bad rating. But the issues I had with this book sometimes overcame the good stuff. I can't stop comparing the book to the Netflix movie based on it I saw beforehand (yes, I have watched the movie adaptation before reading the book yet again, AND STILL YOU HAVEN'T SLAYED ME YOU BUFFOONS) and I feel the movie did some things more justice. <br /><br /><i>Self-proclaimed fat girl Willowdean Dickson (dubbed “Dumplin’” by her former beauty queen mom) has always been at home in her own skin. Her thoughts on having the ultimate bikini body? Put a bikini on your body. With her all-American beauty best friend, Ellen, by her side, things have always worked…until Will takes a job at Harpy’s, the local fast-food joint. There she meets Private School Bo, a hot former jock. Will isn’t surprised to find herself attracted to Bo. But she is surprised when he seems to like her back. Instead of finding new heights of self-assurance in her relationship with Bo, Will starts to doubt herself. So she sets out to take back her confidence by doing the most horrifying thing she can imagine: entering the Miss Clover City beauty pageant—along with several other unlikely candidates—to show the world that she deserves to be up there as much as any twiggy girl does. Along the way, she’ll shock the hell out of Clover City—and maybe herself most of all.</i> <br /><br />Starting from the bad, the addition of the love triangle took many things away from the story. First of all, <b>the first 150 pages were completely useless</b>. They were everything about Bo and all this smooch smooch romantic shit and the important storyline of the pageant hadn't even started yet. I'm not saying the romantic part couldn't be the book... but this book wasn't about that. This book was about body positivity and family and friendship and the whole romantic thing, that was emphasized a lot, took points from the story for me. At some point, <b>the pageant story felt like a subplot to the romantic story</b>. I felt like the book was torn in half, one chapter was the love triangle plot and the other half the pageant plot. <b>It was like reading two different books</b>. Confusing af. And come on now, let's be real. Everyone and their mother knew Mitch didn't stand a chance. Come the fuck on.<br /><br /><b>The movie did an incredible job highlighting the true meaning of the story</b>. They completely eliminated Mitch's character and Will's inner struggle of whom she was gonna pick and shit, and gave more screen time to the pageant and the characters and the friendships. It was fucking beautiful. The movie gave me feels the book didn't achieve to. And it's mostly the other way around for me.<br /><br />Now... what I liked. I loved all the characters, they were all unique and quirky and themselves and they all stood out from each other, which is really hard to achieve. They all hard something to add to the table, they all meant something to Will and they all gave us an important lesson to take away. Also, gotta love the diversity. This book was so modern and yet so vintage with the Dolly Parton love and the old feeling I got from it (also the lack of technology talk), and yet so modern because of the theme and the characters. It gave a smile on my face at some parts, that's for sure.<br /><br />Overall, this book would have been a five star read for me if not for the love triangle. Mostly, love triangle don't bother me much but the love triangle in this book brought it down. I want to read the next book, but I will hold myself, for now. Maybe it will become a Netflix movie and will be better than the book again, who knows. Anyway, till the next one K KYE!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11202269094223075863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1251253402" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1251253402" />
    <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata"><img alt="Faye, la Patata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557835753p2/7650833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1251253402?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=inspiring">inspiring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=body-positive">body-positive</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=lovely-romance-but-not-central">lovely-romance-but-not-central</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=finding-oneself">finding-oneself</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=heart-doing-blackflips">heart-doing-blackflips</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=high-school-drama-done-right">high-school-drama-done-right</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1251253402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17446612206031130112"><strong>Once upon a time, I was fat.</strong><br/><br/><strong>I would have liked to use the nicer term "overweight", but who am I kidding?</strong> Almost weighing 70 kilos in my 5 feet 3 inches frame, I was fat and unhappy. I had big fucking boobs, big bulging sides, big buttcheeks, big arms, thighs that met together in at least one tangent, and the fact that my cheeks were already chubby without the added fat? <strong>Unhappiness galore.</strong> I tried to convince myself that even though I looked this way, I should still exude confidence because my p</span>
  <span id="freeText17446612206031130112" style="display:none"><strong>Once upon a time, I was fat.</strong><br><br><strong>I would have liked to use the nicer term "overweight", but who am I kidding?</strong> Almost weighing 70 kilos in my 5 feet 3 inches frame, I was fat and unhappy. I had big fucking boobs, big bulging sides, big buttcheeks, big arms, thighs that met together in at least one tangent, and the fact that my cheeks were already chubby without the added fat? <strong>Unhappiness galore.</strong> I tried to convince myself that even though I looked this way, I should still exude confidence because my physical appearance didn't and shouldn't decide my worth as a person, but after countless, "Oh, dear! Look at how you've <em>grown</em>!" from uncles and aunts who drop by every 2 months, after having to look for pants two to three sizes larger because I gained more weight <em>again</em>, after having seen your friends get hit on and try out sexy-as-fuck clothes and look so effortlessly fabulous, and you were stuck with pants and loose shirts, it started getting <strong>old</strong>, and <strong>fast</strong>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441212070i/16078718._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>It came to that point where whenever I heard the term <em>mataba</em> (fat) or <em>malaki</em> (big), I'd get so insecure and anxious.</strong> I'd want to get out of the scene and then hide until everyone was gone. I'd start thinking how inadequate I was, how much I was missing out on just because I wasn't as sexy or as fabulous as other girls. I'd start crying to myself why the fuck I was this way. Why did my mom had to come from a family of big people? Who didn't my dad come from a family that was tall and glamorous? I struggled so hard during this phase, and it became that motivation for me to shed down the weight, because I didn't want these wordsto keep haunting me like a ghost that just won't go away.<strong> It was mentally, emotionally, and psychologically traumatizing for me.</strong><br><br>I've lost weight then. I've become confident. I feel better now in my own skin and body.<br><br><strong>But I do wish this book had already existed during that time of my life, because maybe I wouldn't have hated myself that much then.</strong> Willowdean is fat, and she doesn't care. I mean, she does feel insecure about herself sometimes (like everybody else does), but she is fairly confident in her own body, although she does struggle with the judging and teasing of her peers when it comes to body types that are not deemed "beautiful" by society. Willow sets out to change that, by joining a beauty pageant, and inspiring deemed "fat/queer" girls to join her as well.<br><br>I loved Will's character and attitude. She was a mix of the ME I was back then, and the ME that I wish I was back then. <strong>Her insecurities were the things that I was anxious about on a daily basis, the only difference is that Willow decided to do something about it, and to prove to others wrong that someone's being fat is not a cause for them to not do the things they want to do. </strong>That just become someone is queer doesn't mean they can't win a fucking beauty pageant. That just become someone has a buckteeth doesn't mean they can't feel and be beautiful. This was a light-hearted book that talked about heavy issues and made them inspiring, enlightening, and so, so positive.<br><br><strong>I used to be fat, and I used to be ashamed of it. Willow made me realize just how wrong I was for feeling so, for letting people's opinions weigh me down and decide how worthy I was. Fat is just an adjective, but that doesn't make up the whole of me.</strong><br><br>Aside from the strong messages that was in this book, I was in awe of the female friendships and family dynamics that were portrayed here, and how much Will has grown so much as a character through these unexpected bonds. There were so many complex themes that played out between each and every one of them - the relationship between a fat daughter and a mother who was still stuck in her glorious days as a beauty pageant winner; between two best friends who come from two opposite sides of the spectrum; between a girl and a boy whose worlds are far apart; among four females who were shunned as outcasts because of how they looked. I loved each and every one of them, and how positive this book made them out be. <strong>Yes, there were drama, but it wasn't the exhausting kind where you'd want to haul the book into the trash can. They were the kind that tingled and pulled your heart a little bit, then warmed you all over.</strong><br><br>Plus, there's a ship that unexpectedly made me want to clutch my heart. A romance rarely does that to me.<br><br>Dumplin' is something to behold. <strong>It speaks to every one of us who have felt insecure and frustrated with ourselves - by the way we look, or the way we act, or simply because by the way we simply <em>are, </em>all insecurities brought about by social pressure and norms.</strong> It speaks to that side of us who looked for reasons to feel confident in ourselves. This book gives that to you and lets you realize that at the end of the day, we're not made up by the labels society imposes upon us. I am me because of the experiences, values, and things that make up me; and you are you for the same reasons, too<strong>. Fat, or short, or queer, or straight, or thin, or healthy - who the fuck cares? Let's not make these things <em>define</em> us. Life is so much more than that.</strong><br><br><strong>This book makes you want to scream, "Yeah, I used to be fat! Maybe in the future I'll get fat again! But you know what? FUCK THAT SHIT CAUSE EITHER WAY I'M BEAUTIFUL!"</strong></span>
  <a data-text-id="17446612206031130112" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2723854785" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2723854785" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2723854785?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062327192" href="/book/show/30653682-dumplin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2723854785" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17531390683183943305"><b>
  <i>‘all my life i have had a body worth commenting on and if living in my skin has taught me anything its that if its not your body, its not yours to comment on.’</i>
</b><br/><br/>this is a book i wish i had in high school but a story i can still appreciate today. in fact, anyone who has ever had insecurities or issues with their body (which is literally everyone) should read this. <br/><br/>there are such a wholesome messages in this book - how loyalty is the key to meaningful friendship, no one can love you until you lo</span>
  <span id="freeText17531390683183943305" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>‘all my life i have had a body worth commenting on and if living in my skin has taught me anything its that if its not your body, its not yours to comment on.’</i>
</b><br /><br />this is a book i wish i had in high school but a story i can still appreciate today. in fact, anyone who has ever had insecurities or issues with their body (which is literally everyone) should read this. <br /><br />there are such a wholesome messages in this book - how loyalty is the key to meaningful friendship, no one can love you until you love yourself, true beauty is who you are and not what you look like - that i am able to overlook some of the slight negatives that stood out. because the idea of body positivity is one that i am super passionate about and something that needs to be represented in literature more often. <br /><br />i love how this story explores and really praises the fact that everyone comes in different shapes, sizes, colours but that doesnt mean people arent special or important because of it. it doesnt mean beauty is a set standard. it doesnt mean those who look a certain way are better than others. <br /><br />it means we are all unique and lovely and wonderful. it means those who think otherwise are not worth thinking about at all. and it means that you are the best you that only you can be.<br /><br />so in the wise words of queen dolly parton herself - find out who you are and do it on purpose. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17531390683183943305" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1381047621" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1381047621" />
    <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar"><img alt="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530646317p2/11183856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1381047621?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1381047621" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5472087731396226297">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/><b>EDIT FOR INDEPENDENCE DAY RE-READ (BECAUSE WHAT ELSE IS A HOLIDAY FOR IF NOT TO CHANNEL YOUR INNER SLOTH AND READ TWO BOOKS IN ONE DAY????): Bumping to 5 Stars because there ain't nothing more 'Murican than Texas, beauty pageants and Dolly Parton.</b><br/><br/><br/><b>BUUUUUUUUUMP!!!!!!!!!! Because this premieres on Netflix tonight and I'm so excited to go home, put my PJs on, cozy up in bed, turn on the boobtube and shove my face full of what I lovingly ca</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5472087731396226297" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br><b>EDIT FOR INDEPENDENCE DAY RE-READ (BECAUSE WHAT ELSE IS A HOLIDAY FOR IF NOT TO CHANNEL YOUR INNER SLOTH AND READ TWO BOOKS IN ONE DAY????): Bumping to 5 Stars because there ain't nothing more 'Murican than Texas, beauty pageants and Dolly Parton.</b><br><br><br><b>BUUUUUUUUUMP!!!!!!!!!! Because this premieres on Netflix tonight and I'm so excited to go home, put my PJs on, cozy up in bed, turn on the boobtube and shove my face full of what I lovingly call "diabetes in a bag" like my faaaaaaaaar removed teenage self . . . . </b><br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544198353i/26709415.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>ORIGINAL REVIEW:</b><br><br>Most of my friends gave this one a “meh” rating, but I FREAKING LOOOOOOOOVED it . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452875633ra/17755418.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>They obviously all read it wrong (j/k). They also might have actually ponied up some dollars for it, but it was gifted to me by a <i>wee tipsy</i> witch on Festivus Eve.<br><br>Meet Willowdean Dickson . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“That’s me. I’m fat. It’s not a cuss word. It’s not an insult. At least it’s not when I say it. So I always figure why not get it out of the way?”</i>
</b><br><br>Remind you of anyone?????<br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452875633ra/17755419.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Yep. Me too. It didn’t take long, however, to realize that Willowdean’s sassy persona was merely a front and that she was your average, insecure, teenaged girl. And I loved her. In a world of YA where the characters’ voices sound older than a geezer like me it was refreshing to read someone so realistic. <br><br>So what was Willowdean’s story about? Well, pull up a chair and let me <s>fangirl</s> tell you. Willowdean (or Dumplin’ as her momma calls her) is a plus-sized 16 year old who lives waaaaaay down South in Texas with her momma, a former beauty queen and current organizer of her small town’s annual local pageant . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452875633ra/17755420.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>When not attending school or hanging with her bestie Ellen, Will works part-time at the local Harpy’s – which my brain <b>WOULD. NOT. STOP.</b> calling “Hardee’s” and I’ve been craving a monster thickburger ever since . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452875633ra/17755421.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>(You’re welcome, fellas)<br><br>Anywho. Needless to say, Willowdean’s day-to-day is not one filled with thrills and chills. That is until her new co-worker “Private School Bo” takes an interest in her . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“My first kiss, which took place behind a Harpy’s Burgers &amp; Dogs and next to a dumpster full of day-old trash. Yes, it was perfect.”</i>
</b><br><br>It was perfect until Will realizes that Bo will be switching schools and apparently their summer romance wasn’t quite what she thought it was . . . .<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452875633ra/17755422.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>(*insert sad face*)<br><br>And that’s when Willowdean decides enough is enough and it’s high time people get treated like people no matter what their size. How is she going to bridge the gap between fat and thin? Why, by entering the Miss Clover City beauty pageant, of course. But she can’t do it on her own . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452875633ra/17755423.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book may not have been perfect, but I gobbled it right up anyway. My only real complaint? The romance. I realize that the heart wants what it wants (thank you, Selena Gomez), but does it always have to be <i>this</i> guy???? <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452875633ra/17755424.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>(*cough douche cough*)<br><br>Why can’t it be <b>this</b> guy every once in awhile????<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452875633ra/17755425.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Realistically, if I were a teenager again I’d probably be shallow and go for the hot one too so I can’t get too angry. Especially if he said stuff like this . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“Willowdean Opal Dickson, you are beautiful. Fuck anyone who’s ever made you feel anything less.”</i>
</b> <br><br>Plus, when complete and total <b>A.W.E.S.O.M.E.</b> is also contained within the pages . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452875633ra/17755426.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Nearly anything can be forgiven. It’s time every girl realizes . . . <br><br><b>
  <i>“There’s a beauty queen in that cute, little fat girl.”<br><br>“No,” I say. “That cute little fat girl IS a beauty queen.”</i>
</b><br><br>And then when you grow up? You can <b>REALLY</b> be brave . . . <br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://vimeo.com/125347592">https://vimeo.com/125347592</a><br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452875633ra/17755427.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>My friend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1383418588?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna</a> liked this one even more than I did and wrote up a great review. Go check it out.</span>

<div id="review_1347340020" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1347340020" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1347340020?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=sugar-spice-n-everything-nice">sugar-spice-n-everything-nice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=hate-the-characters-hate-the-book">hate-the-characters-hate-the-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=protagonists-i-want-to-laser-face">protagonists-i-want-to-laser-face</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=watch-out-for-puddles-of-angst">watch-out-for-puddles-of-angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=great-concept-poor-execution">great-concept-poor-execution</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=typical">typical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=girl-squad">girl-squad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1347340020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1131755897549187274"><b>2.5 stars </b> <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"If you're gonna go, then go<br/>She said to me on the phone<br/>So tired of hearin' all your<br/>Boy problems<br/>If you're gonna stay then stay<br/>He's not gonna change anyway<br/>So tired of hearin' all your<br/>Boy problems"</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442057858ra/16187853.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Dumplin' is about Dolly Parton and I opened with a Carly Rae Jepsen song. One, because I'm not familiar with Dolly's music. Two, Boy Problems describes Dumplin' perfectly. I'd wager half the book is angst over boys and romance instead of the promised pageant revolution. <br/><br/>Willowdean is fat—an</span>
  <span id="freeText1131755897549187274" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars </b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"If you're gonna go, then go<br>She said to me on the phone<br>So tired of hearin' all your<br>Boy problems<br>If you're gonna stay then stay<br>He's not gonna change anyway<br>So tired of hearin' all your<br>Boy problems"</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442057858ra/16187853.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Dumplin' is about Dolly Parton and I opened with a Carly Rae Jepsen song. One, because I'm not familiar with Dolly's music. Two, Boy Problems describes Dumplin' perfectly. I'd wager half the book is angst over boys and romance instead of the promised pageant revolution. <br><br>Willowdean is fat—and she knows it. She doesn't go on unnecessary diets to change herself and is comfortable enough to slip on a swimsuit and go swimming with her bestie.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"There's something about swimsuits that make you think you've got to earn the right to wear them. Really, the criteria is simple. Do you have a body? Put a swimsuit on it."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Then she meets a boy at work, Bo, commonly referred to as Peachbutt because he's a fine slice of fruit on a summer's day. Nearing the school year, she breaks up with him because she can't stand the stares that comes with a fat girl dating a cute guy.<br><br>Here's where Dumplin' falls apart for me. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442057858ra/16187854.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Based on the blurb, <b>I anticipated Willowdean to be a sassmaster confident in her own skin.</b> Instead I get an <b>angsty insecure mess</b> told in a, frankly, <b>run-of-the-mill YA heroine narrative voice.</b> I wanted punch and fizz and got milk and cinnamon. <br><br>There's nothing wrong with feeling inadequate about your body. It's a natural feeling and on any other occasion, I would be thrilled to see it addressed in such a relatable manner. <br><br>But it's not what I ordered. It's not what the blurb promised. For once, I wanted to read a book narrated by a heavyset girl who doesn't give two fucks about her weight or what strangers think. And joins a beauty pageant to show 'em fat-bottomed girls make the rockin' world go round.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442057858ra/16187855.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Willowdean doesn't join the pageant until halfway through and that's after endless fluffy moments and boring everyday occurrences. <b>The pacing is ridiculously slow. </b> I didn't expect romance to make up a huge chunk and for it to be utter <b>wish-fulfillment</b>. Seriously, what are the odds of two guys—one hot loner (Bo) and a football player (Mitch)—being interested in the same girl? <br><br>Willowdean <b>leads Mitch on</b>, let's get that out of the way. No, it's not a matter of male privilege. Willowdean has done squat to demonstrate she's not interested in him, despite pining for Peachbutt. They've gone on on dates, they've held hands, they've kissed—she freaking writes his name on her face in permanent marker to ask him to the Sadie Hawkins dance.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I shouldn't but I move to kiss [Bo]. My nerves hum and this moment when my body feels both chaotic and determined is what was missing with Mitch."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442057858ra/16187856.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's selfish, disgusting, and destroyed any redeeming qualities this book had, like female friendships and a positive outlook on sex.<br><br>Ultimately, I'd compare Dumplin' to Meghan Trainor's hit All About That Bass. It attempts to promote a body-positive message, but <a href="http://jennytrout.com/?p=7857" rel="nofollow noopener">ends up shading women who aren't curvy.</a> Dumplin' had the ingredients for success and squandered them. <br><br>What a waste of potential. <br><br><i>ARC provided by Edelweiss. All quotes taken from an uncorrected galley proof and may be subject to change.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1131755897549187274" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_3352888516" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3352888516" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3352888516?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=first-love">first-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=competition">competition</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3352888516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3031211545412895342">I was selected to compete for the title of Miss Canada, a personality contest, in March 2021, but I have no experience with pageants so I decided to read this book in case it could illuminate me a little. Miss Canada is not a beauty pageant, but the presentation is still important. You don’t have to be the prettiest to win but you do need to look polished.<br/><br/>Will’s opinion of pageants is not very positive, so I’m not sure just how good an idea reading this was, but she does make these contests soun</span>
  <span id="freeText3031211545412895342" style="display:none">I was selected to compete for the title of Miss Canada, a personality contest, in March 2021, but I have no experience with pageants so I decided to read this book in case it could illuminate me a little. Miss Canada is not a beauty pageant, but the presentation is still important. You don’t have to be the prettiest to win but you do need to look polished.<br /><br />Will’s opinion of pageants is not very positive, so I’m not sure just how good an idea reading this was, but she does make these contests sound like memorable experiences. I was excited before, because it sounds challenging and completely different from anything I’ve ever done, but I’m even more excited now.<br /><br />Whether I win or not, I’ll always have the dresses I’ll wear and the memories that will be associated with them. And hopefully, there will be more camaraderie than competition between us girls. There is limited camaraderie in this book, mostly because the pageant takes actually much less space in the story than Will’s romantic life but I absolutely adored her and her mother’s interactions, good and bad. In the end, the family theme had more impact on me than the friendship and romance ones.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a>Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3031211545412895342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17454316981690104770">I had such high hopes for this book but it was just.... average. The characters weren't amazing, the story wasn't amazing, etc. I was really excited to read this because I love reading books about fat girls, but her size was rarely mentioned. I know the book isn't supposed to focus on her weight, but I found it a little less relatable than i'd like because it failed to give descriptions of her size. Like at one point near the end of the book, it was talking about how she pulled her knees up to h</span>
  <span id="freeText17454316981690104770" style="display:none">I had such high hopes for this book but it was just.... average. The characters weren't amazing, the story wasn't amazing, etc. I was really excited to read this because I love reading books about fat girls, but her size was rarely mentioned. I know the book isn't supposed to focus on her weight, but I found it a little less relatable than i'd like because it failed to give descriptions of her size. Like at one point near the end of the book, it was talking about how she pulled her knees up to her chest and the fat girl in me just went nuh-uh. my knees haven't touched my chest in 17 years. But anyway, this book was just forgettable, and it makes me sad because I was really looking forward to this. Nothing about it was grand and spectacular, and although I liked the writing style, I wish it could have been tweaked to pack more of a punch. The beauty pagaent that this book centers around took place in like 20 pages and there was barely any explanation about it. <br /><br />I would still suggest reading this, but if this is one of your most anticipated books of 2015 like it was for me, you might work on lowering those expectations right about now.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1588710164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11915492692591257828"><b>4.25 stars!</b> <br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/C26BD86C-1589-4719-9164-7242DB627E3C_zpsyp8jlntu.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475226489i/20697581._SX540_.png' alt=' photo C26BD86C-1589-4719-9164-7242DB627E3C_zpsyp8jlntu.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Find out who you are and do it on purpose” -Dolly Parton </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/>Dumplin’ was one of those books I devoured. When I listen to an audio book, I know I’m really into it when I have great books sitting on my kindle waiting for me to read, but I’m finding inconsequential tasks to do around the house just so I can listen. It took me less than 2 days to listen to this book, which is super fast for me. There are so many parts in this story that were relatable to me. I adored our he</span>
  <span id="freeText11915492692591257828" style="display:none"><b>4.25 stars!</b> <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/C26BD86C-1589-4719-9164-7242DB627E3C_zpsyp8jlntu.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475226489i/20697581._SX540_.png" alt=" photo C26BD86C-1589-4719-9164-7242DB627E3C_zpsyp8jlntu.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Find out who you are and do it on purpose” -Dolly Parton </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Dumplin’ was one of those books I devoured. When I listen to an audio book, I know I’m really into it when I have great books sitting on my kindle waiting for me to read, but I’m finding inconsequential tasks to do around the house just so I can listen. It took me less than 2 days to listen to this book, which is super fast for me. There are so many parts in this story that were relatable to me. I adored our heroine, Ms. Willowdean Dixon. <br><br>Our leading lady has an ex-beauty queen mother, her best friend Ellen, and an addiction to all things Dolly Parton. She’s in high school and has just recently started working at Harpy’s, a local fast food joint. It’s there that she meets Bo. Bo used to be a jock and is someone Will is attracted to. She’s shocked when she finds out he likes her too. This story has an element of romance, which I loved, but that’s not what the story was about. It was, more than anything, a story of acceptance and self discovery. <br><br>Willowdean doesn’t have the same body most of her friends do. I wouldn’t say she’s fine or happy with it, she has insecurities just like everyone else, but slowly she embraces who she is. She realizes that no one has the right to comment on anyones body but their own. <br><i>
  <blockquote>“All my life I’ve had a body worth commenting on and if living in my skin has taught me anything it’s that if it’s not your body, it’s not yours to comment on.” </blockquote>
</i><br>Will decides, to prove a point, she will enter the beauty pageant her mother once won and helps run every year. Along with a fun group of misfit girls from her high school, she makes a stand. I grew to love this group of girls and the effect they had on Willowdean. There was so much I loved about this book. I could feel all of Will’s insecurities as if they were my own. I loved watching her grown and triumph. It was a pretty perfect story. If only the ending wasn’t so rushed. I feel as a romance reader, I’m pretty spoiled when it comes to epic HEA’s and fantastic epilogues. And I liked the way it ended, I did… but I wanted more! Either way, this was a great read. Probably one of the best YA’s I’ve read this year. If it wasn’t for the ending not giving me as much as I wanted, it would have been a 5. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/8BDE4BDE-8260-4EA7-BE2F-E37307FF6C86_zpshmdl9gby.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475226489i/20697582._SX540_.png" alt=" photo 8BDE4BDE-8260-4EA7-BE2F-E37307FF6C86_zpshmdl9gby.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_2597023599" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2597023599" />
    <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court"><img alt="High Lady of The Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556501727p2/62560505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2597023599?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court?shelf=contemporary-read">contemporary-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2597023599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2749730834220675014">Before I get into my review, I haven’t watched the movie yet, so if you have any thoughts on the movie, or the movie in relation to the book, leave your thoughts in the comments because I have to make up my mind about whether to watch the movie or not, and I would love to talk to you guys about it.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>"I’m Dumplin’. And Will and Willowdean. I’m fat. I’m happy. I’m insecure. I’m bold."</i>
</b><br/><br/>This is a book about confidence, friendship, and being comfortable in your own skin. It’s a book about teenage, g</span>
  <span id="freeText2749730834220675014" style="display:none">Before I get into my review, I haven’t watched the movie yet, so if you have any thoughts on the movie, or the movie in relation to the book, leave your thoughts in the comments because I have to make up my mind about whether to watch the movie or not, and I would love to talk to you guys about it.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"I’m Dumplin’. And Will and Willowdean. I’m fat. I’m happy. I’m insecure. I’m bold."</i>
</b><br /><br />This is a book about confidence, friendship, and being comfortable in your own skin. It’s a book about teenage, growing up, and growing apart.<br /><br />Dumplin’ was a very impulsive read for me. I hadn’t planned to start reading it anytime soon, in fact the list of books I have planned to read is growing exponentially by the moment. I opened the book fearing the worst, that it would be an overly emotional story about a girl depressed about herself and everything she goes through, because I did not remember the blurb from when I read it last year, which I must say is becoming quite typical of me. In all honesty, this book was an amazing reading. I started it and finished it very quickly, the story moves at a great pace, and the protagonist is great while not being unrealistic.<br /><br />I can’t get over how beautifully realistic this book is. The high school background, the characters, the situations they’re placed in, and Willowdean herself are extremely naturalistic. Willowdean is an amazing character with a personality to trump all else. While being aware of her weight, Willowdean is never weighed down by her appearance and focuses on being the best possible version of herself. Of course, she is also susceptible to the woes of being in high school, and her mom’s endless efforts to make her lose weight. But through it all she stays true to herself and everything she believes in. She is a determined young woman with the power accomplish whatever she wishes, and I loved that Julie Murphy took the time to show us Willowdean at her most vulnerable to convey that no one, no matter how strong we are, can go through life without feeling the ups and downs.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"I think you gotta be who you want to be until you feel like you are whoever it is you’re trying to become. Sometimes half of doing something is pretending that you can." </i>
</b><br /><br />The setting of the book is pretty typical, in Clover City, Willowdean goes to your typical high school with its typically assorted student bodies. Willowdean’s mother is generally the host of the Miss Clover City beauty pageant, which she won when she was in high school. And every year when Pageant week starts her mother goes all in with the preparations choosing to escape from the reality of what her life has become. In this book, Willowdean’s aunt Lucy is said to have died a while ago and while Willowdean still mourns her aunt’s death her mother seems very emotionally detached from the whole situation.<br /><br />Willowdean and Ellen have been best friends for pretty much their whole lives, it all started when Ellen’s mother and Willowdean’s aunt had once bonded over their love for Dolly Parton, who was a famous singer, and now both Willowdean and Ellen are also big fans. We see Willowdean and Ellen grow slightly apart in this book when the differences in their life become a bit too hard to handle. The bond between friends being a major part of this story, Willowdean and Ellen’s friendship plays a huge role in leading to character growth.<br /><br />We see new friendships formed in this book when Willowdean makes the decision to join the pageant. She inspire the outcasts or unnoticed or the most frequently picked on people in the school to join too. While doing this, her long time crush Bo seems to return her feelings, but their relationship is nothing but eventful. <br /><br />This book was a sweet book about friendship and family and if you haven’t read it yet you should check it out, it might surprise you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2749730834220675014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer886139630119057317"><b> <i> DNF @ 65% </i> </b> <br/><br/>What started off as beautiful body positive book. . .<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492441738i/22517412.jpg' width='400' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i> I’m fat. It’s not a cuss word. It’s not an insult. At least it’s not when I say it. So I always figure why not get it out of the way? </i><br/><br/>and<br/><br/><i> I know that fat girls are supposed to be allergic to pools or whatever, but I love swimming… I know people stare, but they can’t blame me for wanting to cool off…What about having huge, bumpy thighs means that I need to apologize? </i><br/><br/>Slowly turned into…constant judgement ???!!??<br/><br/><i>I’m fat, but Milli</i></span>
  <span id="freeText886139630119057317" style="display:none"><b> <i> DNF @ 65% </i> </b> <br><br>What started off as beautiful body positive book. . .<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492441738i/22517412.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> I’m fat. It’s not a cuss word. It’s not an insult. At least it’s not when I say it. So I always figure why not get it out of the way? </i><br><br>and<br><br><i> I know that fat girls are supposed to be allergic to pools or whatever, but I love swimming… I know people stare, but they can’t blame me for wanting to cool off…What about having huge, bumpy thighs means that I need to apologize? </i><br><br>Slowly turned into…constant judgement ???!!??<br><br><i>I’m fat, but Millie’s the type of fat that requires elastic waist pants because they don’t make pants with buttons and zippers in her size. Her eyes are too close together and her nose pinches up at the end. She wears shirts with puppies and kittens and not in an ironic way. </i><br><br>Which ultimately turned into. . .<br><br><i> My Scientific Opinion: This place is a shithole and all the girls who work here are vapid skanks who treat me like El’s charity case friend. </i><br><br>And we got an open invitation to the Self-Pitying Party. . .<br><br><i> My illusions of our after-school romance are dissolving like vapor… I won’t be ridiculed. I won’t be one-half of the couple who everyone stares at and asks, //How did she get him?// </i><br><br>Omg a hot guy likes you??? But you don’t want him to like you <b>in public</b>??? You won’t even tell your best friend about him bc your jealous she’s making friends besides you ??? and then you blame it on the guy bc CLEARLY he’s at fault???<br><br>hmmmm<br><br>10/10 rational thinking going on here. <br><br>Also love triangle warning ahead. Not only is this fabulous girl able to score her smokin’ hot crush but one of the FOOTBALL players is also checking her out, is there ANYTHING this girl, CAN’T do??!!???<br><br>Anyways, it seems to be a good book but I have 0 energy to put up with the drama that tags along. <br><br>Meh.<br><br>Less judgement, more body positivity and friendship, please. <br><br><i> “I guess sometimes the perfection we perceive in others is made up of a whole bunch of tiny imperfections, because some days the damn dress just won't zip.” </i><br><br>1.5 stars!!! (cause it made me laugh)</span>
