    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1270418517" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1270418517" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1270418517?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1270418517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13783396363919888510"><b>Well, WOW, that was a breath of fresh air.</b> I was freakishly worried about this book because I <i>loathed</i> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15728577.Side_Effects_May_Vary' title='Side Effects May Vary by Julie Murphy' rel='nofollow noopener'>Side Effects May Vary</a>. But you know what? Dumplin' was INCREDIBLE. There were a few things I was pretty squinty about (basically the romance) but it was so realistic and down-to-earth and refreshing and SOUTHERN Y'ALL. (Warning: I am Australia. I don't even know what Southern <i>is</i>. The ya'll's just amuse me.) Oh! Oh! OH! And the best part? It's about a beauty pagent so do you know what comes next?</span>
  <span id="freeText13783396363919888510" style="display:none"><b>Well, WOW, that was a breath of fresh air.</b> I was freakishly worried about this book because I <i>loathed</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15728577.Side_Effects_May_Vary" title="Side Effects May Vary by Julie Murphy" rel="nofollow noopener">Side Effects May Vary</a>. But you know what? Dumplin' was INCREDIBLE. There were a few things I was pretty squinty about (basically the romance) but it was so realistic and down-to-earth and refreshing and SOUTHERN Y'ALL. (Warning: I am Australia. I don't even know what Southern <i>is</i>. The ya'll's just amuse me.) Oh! Oh! OH! And the best part? It's about a beauty pagent so do you know what comes next?<br>DO YA?<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435805174ra/15379874.gif" width="500" height="274" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435816689ra/15380488.gif" width="250" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>Heck yes.<br>(I love that movie, by the way. It is incredible. Also Michael Caine. BUT MOVING ON.)<br><br><b>The characters are downright fabulous.</b> They're not perfect, gosh, they're riddled with flaws, but everyone is interesting and dimensional. I didn't agree with all the characters actions...actually, Willowdean (the protagonist) rubbed me up the wrong way A LOT, but I can't deny how real she felt. I'm pretty sure any girl will relate to her struggles and insecurities. And gosh, she's a <i>character</i>. She introduced her self as "Cashier, Dolly Parton enthusiast, and resident fat girl."<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435816689ra/15380489.gif" width="245" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>She's complex. She's really brave and doesn't give a damn what people think...<i>most of the time</i>. She's still insecure about her body, but -- she wants to be HAPPY in her body. She doesn't want to change. She doesn't believe she should <i>have</i> to change, and I really admired this. She doesn't run around being "preachy" but she stands up for other girls and when a guy catcalls, she yells obscenities back. <b>Willowdean is the kind of protagonist I've LONGED to read about forever.</b> <br><br><b>And the writing? It's very detailed and vivid.</b> Granted, this made for slow reading, though. I'm usually a speed-reader, but I felt I had to physically slow down so I could get all the little snippets. WHICH IS GOOD. I feel like almost every sentence was utilising the sentences and painting pictures and making sure I, as the reader, was totally embroiled in the story. It mad the characters POP too. <br><br><b>OTHER THINGS I REALLY LIKED:</b><br>+ It's not set solely in high school! YAY. Most of the setting, actually, is at the fastfood place they work at.<br>+ It's hilarious when the mother (who is in charge of the pageant) gets all righteous about how it's "not a joke" and how it's "so important" it just reminded me of Miss Congeniality so so much.<br>+ How there's a lot of emphasis on friends! And that growing different and up doesn't have to mean growing apart (though sometimes it can).<br>+ And how it smacked down cliches: like jocks aren't always stupid, and the silent broody guy isn't just beautiful and sexy -- sometimes he's a jerk too.<br>+ How the protagonist was pretty much a normal average person -- school, work, TV, tada. No eccentriciies. (Although I do love eccentric characters, it's nice to have someone more down-to-earth once in a while.) <br>+ Oh and there were tacos.<br><br><b>Okay, but we gotta talk about this cringing romance.</b> It's not a smooth-clean-nice romance, and I GET THAT. It's realistic! When society views you as looking "wrong" (like Willowdean is "fat") then you're going to be plagued by anxieties. But I felt Willowdean was just a bit pathetic about this. And deluded?! Like, she wallows in thinking now one is ever going to love her -- but she basically has two dudes by the end. I MEAN, COME ON. REALLY??? I always feel weird about triangle-type relationships, because one side is always leading someone on and that's unfair and cruel. BUT ANYWAY. So Willowdean meets Bo (which is an adorable name, and reminds me of Po from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3236307.Graceling__Graceling_Realm___1_" title="Graceling (Graceling Realm, #1) by Kristin Cashore" rel="nofollow noopener">Graceling</a>, whom I also adore) at work and they have a tentative summery fling. THEN THEY BREAK UP TRAGICALLY. Why? That is an excellent question, my friends. I have no idea. <b>I don't understand what went wrong between them.</b> And I was focusing! I feel like it was equal parts of fault...Bo wasn't communicating the boundaries of their relationship (like would they continue or break up after summer?) and Willowdean was so OBSESSED with the fact that she was unwantable, that she <i>made</i> herself be unwantable by walking away. <br><br>Like. what.<br><br>(Anyway, I could be wrong about my analysation of their feelings. It was just so confusing for me to read.)<br><br><b>Willowdean is very self-centred.</b> Which was hard to read about, because I can't really fathom how you can exist <i>so deep in your own bubble</i> that you miss what's going on. She has a mega-fight with her best friend (over selfish reasons) and she loses the boy she loves...all because it's all about HER?! I really struggled with this.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1435816689ra/15380490.gif" width="245" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>But otherwise, I feel like this is a super EMPOWERING book!</b> It left me feeling encouraged! It left me with an epic list of quotes that I want to just, possibly, eat because they were so good. It was just so refreshing to read about a girl who isn't skinny but that's not <i>who</i> she is (like she's not enslaved by food through this book, actually, no binge-eating or purging). She's just a teen trying to find her way in the world. And she messes up SO BAD. But that's also realistic. And the ending is unexpected, a little bittersweet, and heartwarming. Although the romance is TOTALLY left hanging. But whatever. <b>I'm pleased with this Dumplin. I am.</b><br><br>***NOTABLE QUOTES OF AWESOME ****<br><i>These quotes are from an ARC and should not be elsewhere, okay, yeah? I'm probs evil for posting them here BUT I CAN'T HELP IT. They be so good.</i><br><br><blockquote>"There was some old guy catcallin' from the drive-thru. Called me sweetcheeks."<br>"Awww," she says. "Well, that's kind of flattering if you think about it."<br>"Mama, come on. No, that's gross."</blockquote><br><br>(Bless this Willowdean.)<br><br><blockquote>"Plus having sex doesn't make you a woman. That is so freaking cliche. If you want to have sex, have sex, but don't make it this huge thing that carries all this weight. You're setting yourself up for disappointment."</blockquote><br><blockquote>I understand that life after highschool is probably something I should be thinking about, but I can't picture me in college and I don't know how to plan for something I can't imagine.</blockquote><br><blockquote>I take one deep breath as I check the to-go bag supply underneath the register. "It's been a long day. Need some space."<br>Marcus mumbles something about PMS and to my surprise, from the kitchen, Bo says, "Why can't she just be having a shitty day? You don't need to make up some bullshit reason why."</blockquote><br><blockquote>"You're missing out on so much." She takes a step toward me. "Boys and dating. That kind of stuff."<br>I scrub my hands down my face. "You have got to be kidding me. News flash, Mom: a man will not cure my troubles."</blockquote><br><blockquote>I hear things like, "so horrible" or "I'm sorry, but she's hideous" or "why doesn't she get braces?"<br>That last one is the sentiment that stays with me all day because Hannah shouldn't have to get braces. Maybe she can't afford them or maybe she's scared to get them. Either way, she shouldn't have to fill her mouth with metal so that some shitheads will leave her alone.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="13783396363919888510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7084447178850502527" style="display:none">I JUST FINISHED THE MOVIE AND IT WAS AMAZING!! It was just as beautiful as the book and, okay, I admit it.... It made me cry 😢 😂<br>*****<br>I'm so happy with Young Adult literature today. Even though it all ranges from space to the forests, but it usually has the same over arching message:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1541952991ra/26579011.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And it's true. Everyone is beautiful. It doesn't matter if you black or white; gay or straight; Christian or Muslim; Big or small. It's about what's in your heart. As long as you fight against the evil and unkind, you are amazing. <br><br>🎵<i>Red and yellow; Black and white. They are precious in his sight. Jesus loves the little children of the WORLD!</i> Lol, sorry for the random burst of song. <br><br>Now, let's talk book! This is a rom-com, which is one of my favorite genres. But! (And it's a big but.) I felt like the book barely focused on the romance and more on Willow Dean learning to love herself, which is fine. I just wish it hadn't been branded as a rom-com.<br><br>So the romance: It was... How do you say it? Bleh. Yes, bleh. First of all because it's a subplot and so I didn't find myself caring about it at all but when I did, I cared for the wrong relationship. I hated Beau (Or is it spelled 'Bo'? I listened to the audiobook so I have no idea.). I found him annoying, stupid, and overall a jerk. Mitch on the other hand was kind, funny and caring. He was perfect for Willow Dean. But no, everyone has to fall in love with the hot stud.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441157415ra/16071245.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Of course, when Beau and WD weren't making out (😖), WD was working on her self love by entering a pageant. Yay! Also, am I the only one who felt like WD's mom was like an evil stepmother. Is this secretly a Cinderella re-telling? <br><br>Also, also that ending was really abrupt. It was just bam! <div id="review_2609515246" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2609515246" />
    <a title="Katie B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49444196-katie-b"><img alt="Katie B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469412116p2/49444196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2609515246?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie B" href="/user/show/49444196-katie-b">Katie B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062327208" href="/book/show/24331435-dumplin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=texas">texas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49444196-katie-b?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2609515246" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer846511279726872963">This was a nice surprise! I really wasn't expecting to like this one as much as I did. I was kinda iffy on whether or not I was going to like the beauty pageant parts of the story but thankfully there were some good moments with that and also the other things going on in the main character's life.<br/><br/>What I loved most about the book was Willowdean wasn't perfect. She could be shallow, cruel, and hypocritical among other things. I found it refreshing to have a protagonist who could act like a jerk. T</span>
  <span id="freeText846511279726872963" style="display:none">This was a nice surprise! I really wasn't expecting to like this one as much as I did. I was kinda iffy on whether or not I was going to like the beauty pageant parts of the story but thankfully there were some good moments with that and also the other things going on in the main character's life.<br /><br />What I loved most about the book was Willowdean wasn't perfect. She could be shallow, cruel, and hypocritical among other things. I found it refreshing to have a protagonist who could act like a jerk. This to me is much more realistic than the usual way YA fiction authors write their main characters. It's like they think if the character is overweight than they can't have any flaws and they become these weird caricatures that don't really resemble anyone I know. It was refreshing to have a main character who lacked self-awareness at times. I look back on growing up and even though I like to think of myself as a good person there were definitely times when I acted in a way that didn't paint me in the best light. For most of us, being a teenager was not always a good time because you are this giant mess of insecurity, raging hormones, and a mind that's not fully developed. And even though you know might know better, you still act like an ass. And big surprise, just because you are overweight doesn't make you immune from being an ass from time to time. So kudos to the author for having a main character with flaws!<br /><br />I absolutely loved how Mitch factored into the story. I found myself reflecting back to crazy high school love life drama and remember exactly how it felt to be not just in Mitch's shoes but Willowdean's as well. It's not fun on either side of the equation. <br /><br />Overall, this was a really enjoyable read but maybe it's not for everyone. I guess it just depends on how you view the main character. Some of the characteristics of her personality that I found endearing, could be annoying for another reader. Not every book or character works for everyone, but for me this was a good fit. I look forward to watching the Netflix movie and also reading the followup to this novel which features some of the side characters in this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="846511279726872963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1582365155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1582365155" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2544584-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442501340p2/2544584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1582365155?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/2544584-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1582365155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15456824369793047380">Dumplin’ is the story of Willowdean Dickson, a fat girl from a small town that hosts the oldest beauty pageant in Texas. After the sudden death of her beloved aunt, Will decides to honor her memory by signing up for the pageant. She wants to try something that her aunt had always denied herself because of her own insecurities about her weight. Now Will suddenly finds herself contending with becoming a beauty queen, her crazy pageant mother, an angry best friend, two cute boys… and maybe a small </span>
  <span id="freeText15456824369793047380" style="display:none">Dumplin’ is the story of Willowdean Dickson, a fat girl from a small town that hosts the oldest beauty pageant in Texas. After the sudden death of her beloved aunt, Will decides to honor her memory by signing up for the pageant. She wants to try something that her aunt had always denied herself because of her own insecurities about her weight. Now Will suddenly finds herself contending with becoming a beauty queen, her crazy pageant mother, an angry best friend, two cute boys… and maybe a small revolution. <br /><br />Full disclosure, I know Julie, and love her very much as a person. She is also, however, an excellent writer. The writing in Dumplin’ is as funny and self-assured as its narrator. From the first sentence I was so immersed in the world that I felt myself dripping with Texas summer sweat. Willowdean, in particular, feels wonderfully real. She’s not cripplingly insecure, but she’s not superhumanly confidant either. Just like most of us! I loved her so much, and got so caught up in her story, that I had to buy an extra charger at the airport. There was NO WAY I was going to let my kindle die without knowing how the whole thing ended.<br /><br />Essential reading for everyone who has ever felt uncomfortable in their own skin… which is everyone. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15456824369793047380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1315364780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1315364780" />
    <a title="Caroline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38672507-caroline"><img alt="Caroline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474291977p2/38672507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1315364780?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline" href="/user/show/38672507-caroline">Caroline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38672507-caroline?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1315364780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer359553719967709473">SO this rating is probably closer to <b>2.5 stars</b> but I decided to round it down because, even though I enjoyed this book, it has too many flaws to be worth a three star rating. <br/><br/>My main problem with this was that it was heralded as a book about body positivity and acceptance but it felt far from it. I found Willowdean to be quite a hypocritical character in general. Her internal monologue was filled with her judging other people; Millie, for example, who Willow points out as <i>'the type of fat that r</i></span>
  <span id="freeText359553719967709473" style="display:none">SO this rating is probably closer to <b>2.5 stars</b> but I decided to round it down because, even though I enjoyed this book, it has too many flaws to be worth a three star rating. <br /><br />My main problem with this was that it was heralded as a book about body positivity and acceptance but it felt far from it. I found Willowdean to be quite a hypocritical character in general. Her internal monologue was filled with her judging other people; Millie, for example, who Willow points out as <i>'the type of fat that requires elastic waist pants because they don't make pants with buttons and zippers in her size'</i>. I was even more frustrated that Willow was annoyed and indignant when another student was made fun of. I honestly saw Willow as no better than the other students- the only difference was that Willow didn't bully them to their face. I don't think that saying she was ashamed to admit something makes it even slightly better. She judges other people to make herself feel better. Rather than eliciting sympathy from me, I was appalled by Willow for being such a judgement butt-head. <br /><br />Furthermore, Willowdean bragged about being confident in her own skin (yaasss you go gurl!) but resorted to shaming other people and their bodies. As I mentioned before, she makes fun of Millie on page three (!!!!) to make herself feel better for not being 'that kind of fat'. What? She also shames skinny people, referring to one as a 'twiggy bitch'. Having read this book, I now understand the comparison drawn between it and that annoying 'All About That Bass' song. The basic message seemed to be that being curvy is okay, and being confident is even better, but fuck skinny girls. I just couldn't get past the hypocrisy of it. <br /><br />(I should point out that I don't think Willow is a bad character because she is insecure or flawed. I am insecure so I understand that facet of her. I found it frustrating that she was so judgmental of other people's insecurities. It was a really unlikable trait for her character to have.)<br /><br />It also frustrated me to no end how when Ellen decides to be supportive and enter the pageant with her, Willow gets all shitty and tells her to drop out. Your friend is trying to support you and you tell her that her support isn't wanted. WHAT?! As Ellen says <i>"You can’t pick and choose who joins the revolution.”</i> I would have thought that standing strong and united with your best friend would be ideal, but apparently not. <br /><br />I did enjoy the last portion of the book. I enjoyed the pageant and the drama surrounding it. As a whole, this book was entertaining. I liked parts of it but found Willow annoying like 80% of the time. I found the love triangle to be kind of unnecessary; her friendship with Mitch was great and I liked it but I don't think complicating it with romance achieved anything. This book was meant to be about Willow overcoming the judgement to be her most confident self, not picking which boy she liked more. Some of the parts about grief and growing up were touching and lovely. Favourite character award is a tie between Millie and Ellen because they were awesome. I don't know if I'd recommend this book to people, but I won't warn them away from it either.</span>
  <a data-text-id="359553719967709473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2099594478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2099594478" />
    <a title="enqi ☁️✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41427900-enqi"><img alt="enqi ☁️✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604082105p2/41427900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2099594478?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="enqi ☁️✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="enqi ☁️✨" href="/user/show/41427900-enqi">enqi ☁️✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24957546-dumplin">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=on-my-kindle">on-my-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41427900-enqi?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2099594478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12211432598235839984">with all the hype surrounding <i> Dumplin' </i>, i'm really sorry to say this book didn't appeal to me at all. i did find the premise interesting and promising at first... but by the time i reached the 60% mark, i was mostly bored and skimming the pages. i have many things to say about it, so let me just make a list of the reasons i <s> hated </s> disliked this book:<br/><br/>1. this book was such a fucking hypocritical mess. <br/><blockquote> <i> Beautiful, he says. Fat, I think. But can't I be both at the same time? </i> </blockquote><br/>what started out as</span>
  <span id="freeText12211432598235839984" style="display:none">with all the hype surrounding <i> Dumplin' </i>, i'm really sorry to say this book didn't appeal to me at all. i did find the premise interesting and promising at first... but by the time i reached the 60% mark, i was mostly bored and skimming the pages. i have many things to say about it, so let me just make a list of the reasons i <s> hated </s> disliked this book:<br /><br />1. this book was such a fucking hypocritical mess. <br /><blockquote> <i> Beautiful, he says. Fat, I think. But can't I be both at the same time? </i> </blockquote><br />what started out as a beautiful book about body positivity soon became the main character, willowdean, imposing her judgements on others and insulting them. it started around 5% (that was quick!) and continued for the rest of the book. <br /><br />2. willowdean was so annoying. like, i-constantly-wanted-to-bash-her-face-in kind of annoying. i am not belittling or reducing her insecurities. in fact, i completely understood her insecurities and related to them, but i expected her to have some character development by the end of the book. but all i got at the end was a love triangle and angst instead of the promised pageant revolution.<br /><br />3. pointless plot. listen, after skimming the blurb any reader would expect our dear willow to win the pageant right? it would be the most fitting end to the story and the most satisfying one, too. "fat" girl defies all stereotypes by winning a beauty pageant, traditional territory of skinny girls with model figures. said plus-sized girl grows into herself and learns to love and accept her body. i was expecting all of that... but then our main girl literally gets herself DQ-ed from the competition. she actually gets disqualified. the worst part is she doesn't even have some grand epiphany to show for it. so what was the whole point of making a plot about a talent pageant and being determined to enter it in order to prove something, if you have nothing to show for it at the end?<br /><br />4. at first i thought her mom was being a bitch by saying she didn't care about entering the pageant and was just doing it for fun, but by the end i was wholeheartedly agreeing with her mom. the pageant featured only when there needed to be some conflict or realisation in the plot. i thought willow had something to prove and she'd work for it, but she didn't even bother doing a talent, or costume, or anything you'd expect of someone who wanted to prove her point. halfway through she even quit on her friends, and then decided to do it again in the end.... honestly enough with the drama.<br /><br />5. love triangle angst. yikes. our girl literally leads the star of the football team on AND yet still manages to snare her hot crush. she has no thought for the other guy's feelings, apparently. next.<br /><br />6. zero plot arc if i haven't said this before. nothing is resolved in the end, everything was rushed to be tied up almost like the author gave up on her own book. willowdean's life doesn't change from when the book started, she doesn't have any visible takeaways from the pageant. when her crush bo asked her to be exclusive, she refused to be because she saw herself as ugly and didn't want to be gossiped about... and at the end of the book she didn't even say yes to him. i expected something. i wanted something to show that she had character development. and there was nothing.<br /><br />oh well. BUT, there are some gems in this book though, and i've highlighted them and made the highlights visible to save you the trouble of reading this book and going through what i did. have a good week ahead everyone!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12211432598235839984" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer9998138977325982774">Dumplin' by Julie Murphy is a book and movie I kept hearing about. I am not one to follow the book trends, I like to read books off the beaten path because I find a lot of hidden gems that way but this book intrigued me. <br/>The story is about a beauty pageant but the overall theme, ironically, is not to judge others, and to be yourself, love yourself, just the way you are!<br/>The characters are great and the plot was predictable but good.   <span id="freeText9998138977325982774" style="display:none">Dumplin' by Julie Murphy is a book and movie I kept hearing about. I am not one to follow the book trends, I like to read books off the beaten path because I find a lot of hidden gems that way but this book intrigued me. <br />The story is about a beauty pageant but the overall theme, ironically, is not to judge others, and to be yourself, love yourself, just the way you are!<br />The characters are great and the plot was predictable but good. I watched the movie after the book. I think the book is geared more for teens since it is more simplified in every aspect. For a grandmother like me and having gone through many of the teen trials and the mother's trials, which the movie seemed to show both of these equally important, I could relate to the movie more. I was laughing one minute then my eyes were leaking the next! ( Darn leaky eyes!)<br />I usually don't read books that cause leaky eyes but this was good, especially for teens and that was what I was reading it for, my young teen grand daughters. I wanted to see if it was good.</span>

<div id="review_1540222667" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1540222667" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1540222667?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=lol">lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=reality-bites">reality-bites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=easy-read">easy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1540222667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11203563570690122608"><b> <i> “There’s something about swimsuits that make you think you’ve got to earn the right to wear them. And that’s wrong. Really, the criteria is simple. Do you have a body? Put a swimsuit on it.” </i></b> <br/><br/>This is one completely adorable, funny, heartwarming and inspiring contemporary YA. I regret that I hadn’t read it sooner. I love the main purpose that the book wants to put across. People spend too much time thinking they’re too fat or too thin, eyes too far apart or too close together, teeth too big or </span>
  <span id="freeText11203563570690122608" style="display:none"><b> <i> “There’s something about swimsuits that make you think you’ve got to earn the right to wear them. And that’s wrong. Really, the criteria is simple. Do you have a body? Put a swimsuit on it.” </i></b> <br /><br />This is one completely adorable, funny, heartwarming and inspiring contemporary YA. I regret that I hadn’t read it sooner. I love the main purpose that the book wants to put across. People spend too much time thinking they’re too fat or too thin, eyes too far apart or too close together, teeth too big or too small, skin too dark or too pale. Perhaps it’s true that somebody else is always going to be better but so what? Nobody is perfect and yes that’s cliché but in order to be comfortable with ourselves, that’s the only way to think. <br /><br /> Every person has insecurities even Jon Snow (no matter how confident, handsome and haaawt he looks *sighs*) and that’s perfectly okay because what a dull life would it be if we all had been so confident and so sure of ourselves all the time. These inspiring ideas were realistically and genuinely portrayed in the story through <b>Dumplin’</b>, the main character who is gorgeous, fat, confident, funny, awkward, beautiful and insecure all at the same time. Her uncertainties about herself are what make her human. They’re what make her relatable and true. I love the statement that she made by entering a pageant. She rocks!<br /><br />The book is another eye-opening experience for me because I’m often guilty of commenting on other people’s body especially when I think they’re too thin. Simple comments like “You really should eat more” seems sweet and harmless to me until I’ve read the book reminding me that I am in no position to comment on anyone’s body unless it’s mine. I think this is a must read for every teenager out there, for everybody actually.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11203563570690122608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1324479976" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1324479976" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)" href="/user/show/16219087-chelsea-chelseadolling-reads">Chelsea (chelseadolling reads)</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1324479976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10485141305221383609">Re-read 5/26/18: I DID IT. I re-read Dumplin’. And I have to say, while I still think Willowdean is honestly the worst, I didn’t hate her with the fire of a thousand suns like I used to. She sucked, but the rest of the book was pretty dang cute and I really liked everyone BUT Willowdean lol. 3.5 stars! Also check out 2015 Chelsea down below trying not to be mean. I hated the book but refused to say so lmao how times change!<br/><br/>Original read 9/22/15: I liked this, but I'd be lying if I said I didn't </span>
  <span id="freeText10485141305221383609" style="display:none">Re-read 5/26/18: I DID IT. I re-read Dumplin’. And I have to say, while I still think Willowdean is honestly the worst, I didn’t hate her with the fire of a thousand suns like I used to. She sucked, but the rest of the book was pretty dang cute and I really liked everyone BUT Willowdean lol. 3.5 stars! Also check out 2015 Chelsea down below trying not to be mean. I hated the book but refused to say so lmao how times change!<br /><br />Original read 9/22/15: I liked this, but I'd be lying if I said I didn't want more from it :/ I feel like there was simultaneously too much and not enough going on. Plus Willowdean (GREAT name though. 10 points for that alone) was a little too bitchy for me. I feel like I'm being too negative. I DID enjoy this. It just wasn't quite what I was hoping for.</span>

<div id="review_1375631977" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1375631977" />
    <a title="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner"><img alt="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588471351p2/7366569.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1375631977?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fafa&#39;s Book Corner" href="/user/show/7366569-fafa-s-book-corner">Fafa&#39;s Book Corner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1375631977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2533834671746165792"><a href='https://fafasbookcorner.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'> Fafa's Book Corner (Wordpress) </a><br/><a href='http://fafasbookcorner.blogspot.ca/' rel='nofollow noopener'> Fafa's Book Corner (Blogger) </a><br/><br/>Beware spoilers ahead!<br/><br/>Updated thoughts:<br/><br/>Dumplin' was read for The Dream Thieves: Badass Broads.<br/><br/>I'm going to be frank I literally only reread this because of the movie. If it hadn't been for the movie, I wouldn't have bothered with this book. Over the last three years I've forgotten so much. To the point where I confused character names and their personalities.<br/><br/>Upon my reread I'm actually surprised that I was even able to finish this! Wi</span>
  <span id="freeText2533834671746165792" style="display:none"><a href="https://fafasbookcorner.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Fafa's Book Corner (Wordpress) </a><br /><a href="http://fafasbookcorner.blogspot.ca/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Fafa's Book Corner (Blogger) </a><br /><br />Beware spoilers ahead!<br /><br />Updated thoughts:<br /><br />Dumplin' was read for The Dream Thieves: Badass Broads.<br /><br />I'm going to be frank I literally only reread this because of the movie. If it hadn't been for the movie, I wouldn't have bothered with this book. Over the last three years I've forgotten so much. To the point where I confused character names and their personalities.<br /><br />Upon my reread I'm actually surprised that I was even able to finish this! Willowdean annoyed me so much. And wow her thoughts were so cringey! For someone who preached body positivity she went against her word so many times! <br /><br />Anyways moving on. So I had many problems with this. I didn't feel that Willowdean's character development was well done. Let alone any of the other characters. The romance was also very cringey. And I didn't see the point of the love triangle. Most of the characters while having real struggles felt two dimensional. I wish we got to know more about their backstories. Would've helped to flesh them out. <br /><br />Onto the things I liked! The beauty pageant was still as entertaining as I remembered. Their girl's friendship was nice. I really liked Mitch. And how some of the topics that were discussed resonated with me. I would've loved to read about Aunt Lucy. I did like the girl power. And despite my issues with these characters I found them to be strong.<br /><br />I'm just so conflicted because there were a lot of good messages! But I never felt that they were done right. Mentioned and just brushed aside. Maybe that's the whole point. I still wanted more. And would've loved to follow other characters aside from Willowdean. <br /><br />Overall I enjoyed some parts and thoroughly disliked others. Regardless I still think it's worth the read. <br /><br />This was recommended by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1261548349" rel="nofollow noopener"> Tash </a>! Click her name to see her review. <br /><br />When I had first read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1261548349" rel="nofollow noopener"> Tash's </a> review I knew that I must read it! I was excepting to love every bit of it and enjoy the story. While I did not love it I did thoroughly enjoy reading it.<br /><br />Willowdean (more often referred to as Will) is one of the fat girls in her town. She has no problem with this and does not consider calling herself fat an insult. Every year her mother and a few others host a beauty pageant. Her mother is a former winner and still fits into the dress she wore when she won.<br /><br />The book starts off during summer right before Will and her best friend Ellen are supposed to go to grade 11. Will works at Harpy's a fast food restaurant. It is revealed that Will has had a crush on Bo her co-worker for some time. Bo doesn't really talk a lot he keeps to himself so it's hard to see whether he likes any of his co-workers in any way.<br /><br />One day as Will is taking the trash out she runs into Bo and he kisses her. Surprised she walks away. He sees her again and apologizes for randomly kissing her and claims that he has some personal stuff going on therefore it would be best not to date anyone. While she isn't happy to hear this she doesn't protest. The next day however he kisses her again. They have a secret relationship for 2 months. No one knows about their relationship and they keep it that way. <br /><br />At that point I was ready to stop reading because the relationship between the two of them was odd and didn't really make sense. But because I bought it and hoping it would get better I read on. I am pretty happy that I did that as it did turn out to be a good story.<br /><br />School is right around the corner so Will assumes that whatever she and Bo have will do done and over with soon. While dropping Ellen to get her payroll she runs into Bo and his family. His stepmother reveals that Bo will start going to Will's school. Will is shocked that she never heard this from Bo. And she can't imagine going to school with him as well as working together.<br /><br />Things aren't so great with her relationship with her mother or Ellen. She feels that her and Ellen are drifting apart mostly because of Ellen's co-worker and new friend Callie who pities Will for being fat. Her aunt passed away recently so it's been hard on both her mother and her. Will felt that her aunt understood her in a way her mother never does. Her aunt and her bonded over some of the silly things her mother said. Her mother is not happy about Will being fat and she tries to subtly push her into losing weight. She does this because she thinks her Will is going to be happier if she loses weight.<br /><br />Now with school beginning the pageant is also right around the corner. Which Will is not at all excited about. She hates the pageant and everything it stands for. After seeing Bo in her history class she decides to quit her job and apply for another one.<br /><br />In a way of moving on from Bo she agrees to go on a date with Mitch who is in her english class. When this fails she enters the pageant. Her entering the pageant inspires 3 other girls to enter with her.<br /><br />This is probably one of the most inspiring books I have ever read! I loved that Will decided to enter the pageant for her aunt and herself. <br /><br />I would have liked to read more about the pageant. I felt that some points in the book the story really dragged. I really did not like how some of the characters tried to shove it down Will's throat that if she lost weight she would be happy. While a lot of people are pretty happy when they lose weight that does not mean that they weren't happy before. This is the case with me. I couldn't really see Will working out with Bo nor Mitch. <br /><br />I was also impressed by the fact that Will did not feel the need to lose weight for the pageant. It was really sweet to read about the other girls entering with her. The friendship was awesome! As well as how complex the characters were and the journey all the girls took with the pageant. I liked how Will repaired her relationship with Ellen and her mother. I was not excepting the book to end the way it did. Kudos to the author for doing something unexpected. <br /><br />Overall this was a really good book! I recommend it to fans of contemporary, Dolly Parton, and anyone looking for an inspiring/empowering book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2533834671746165792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1261548349" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1261548349" />
    <a title="♛Tash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5451856-tash"><img alt="♛Tash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456286012p2/5451856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1261548349?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♛Tash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♛Tash" href="/user/show/5451856-tash">♛Tash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24957546-dumplin">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1261548349" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4429943341495220295"><blockquote>
  <i>"I’m fat. It’s not a cuss word. It’s not an insult. At least it’s not when I say it."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I love this charming book about courage, set in South Texas with a Dolly Parton soundtrack. I was gonna say body image, but truth is, body image is not the central theme of this book. It figures some of course, but it’s more about the courage to retain your shape when the world dictates you to be another.<br/><br/>Willowdean Dickson,<b>Dumplin'</b> to her former beauty queen Mom, is completely fine being fat (not a pejorativ</span>
  <span id="freeText4429943341495220295" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"I’m fat. It’s not a cuss word. It’s not an insult. At least it’s not when I say it."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I love this charming book about courage, set in South Texas with a Dolly Parton soundtrack. I was gonna say body image, but truth is, body image is not the central theme of this book. It figures some of course, but it’s more about the courage to retain your shape when the world dictates you to be another.<br /><br />Willowdean Dickson,<b>Dumplin'</b> to her former beauty queen Mom, is completely fine being fat (not a pejorative term). She’s happy with the fact that she wears drawstring skirts instead of pants for her Harpy’s uniform and being a third-wheel to her bestfriend, El and secretly crushing on fry-cook hottie Private School Bo. She's content with her life until she starts having make-out sessions with Private School Bo. Instead of getting that confidence boost when a crush likes you back, Will finds herself sunk in self-doubt and insecurity.<br /><br />At this point in the book, I also began to doubt myself, am I really as open-minded as I think I am, or am I just a bloody hypocrite? When Bo shows the tiniest bit of interest in Will, I was immediately suspicious of him and was waiting for the big reveal of his ulterior motive, because why else would a hot former jock with sleeve-popping biceps be interested in a fat girl? When a “safer”option in the form of a shy, sweet, plain guy was given to Will, I rooted for him instead<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I terrify you”? The thought of it makes me feel bad, but it’s kind of nice, too. To not feel like the one who’s about the jump out of their skin all the time.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Yes, <b>I am a hypocrite</b>, it is a bitter pill to swallow while reading this otherwise empowering novel. Good thing Julie Murphy isn’t like me, she believes that the fat, the unevenly legged, the bucktoothed girls (and boys) also deserve the hot guy (or girl) and the crown.<br /><br />In her quest to regain the confidence lost from her summer fling with Bo, she decides to join Miss Teen Blue Bonnet. With this, she inspires and alienates the people in her town. This is the part when we see how expertly Julie Murphy writes Will’s character. Will is level-headed, funny and sassy. She has quips like: <i>“liberally spread salad dressing across my plate because on the eight day God created ranch dressing”</i>, but she gets angry when her mother suggests diet and exercise, and she also holds certain prejudice against girls who are fatter than she is. In short, Will is a wonderfully complex character and a witty narrator.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"I think you gotta be who you want to be until you feel like you are whoever is you're trying to become. Sometimes half of doing something is pretending that you can."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />If you are looking for a book that is body &amp; female-friendship positive with a side of romance and humor then add <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18304322.Dumplin_" title="Dumplin' by Julie Murphy" rel="nofollow noopener">Dumplin'</a> to your TBRs people. <b>Add it!</b><br /><br /><i>***arc gifted by the publisher for an honest review***</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4429943341495220295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2300824211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2300824211" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2300824211?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Uo/njpE2IDsqlFbBMWSq7SmNmcFn/rk6FfonqzssQMyzdF1rhu3hHvjswxP7uRvefojRQ2GcK3emElL03lJftw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

When she's not writing or trying to catch stray cats, she works at an academic library. <i>Side Effects May Vary</i> is Julie's debut novel.</span>
